  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7122e4d0-69a7-4921-b292-29e7da55c430'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer13585185106456709266">This is an Alternate Cover edition for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37806657-the-serpent-king' rel='nofollow noopener'>ASIN B00ZNE17D2</a><br/><br/>Dill has had to wrestle with vipers his whole life—at home, as the only son of a Pentecostal minister who urges him to handle poisonous rattlesnakes, and at school, where he faces down bullies who target him for his father’s extreme faith and very public fall from grace.<br/><br/>The only antidote to all this venom is his friends</span>
  <span id="freeText13585185106456709266" style="display:none">This is an Alternate Cover edition for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37806657-the-serpent-king" rel="nofollow noopener">ASIN B00ZNE17D2</a><br /><br />Dill has had to wrestle with vipers his whole life—at home, as the only son of a Pentecostal minister who urges him to handle poisonous rattlesnakes, and at school, where he faces down bullies who target him for his father’s extreme faith and very public fall from grace.<br /><br />The only antidote to all this venom is his friendship with fellow outcasts Travis and Lydia. But as they are starting their senior year, Dill feels the coils of his future tightening around him. The end of high school will lead to new beginnings for Lydia, whose edgy fashion blog is her ticket out of their rural Tennessee town. And Travis is happy wherever he is thanks to his obsession with the epic book series Bloodfall and the fangirl who may be turning his harsh reality into real-life fantasy. Dill’s only escapes are his music and his secret feelings for Lydia—neither of which he is brave enough to share. Graduation feels more like an ending to Dill than a beginning. But even before then, he must cope with another ending—one that will rock his life to the core.<br /><br />Debut novelist Jeff Zentner provides an unblinking and at times comic view of the hard realities of growing up in the Bible Belt, and an intimate look at the struggles to find one’s true self in the wreckage of the past.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13585185106456709266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        $('edition_37806657').observe('prototip:shown', function () {

          });

<a href="/questions/706438-how-much-of-this-book-is-religion-based">How much of this book is religion based?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_706438'><a id="like_count_community_question_706438" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/706438?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F22752127-the-serpent-king">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/30745439-supriya"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1522788691i/30745439._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/30745439-supriya">Supriya</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Given this is set in a small town in the South, there is some fundamentalism (actually pentecostals speaking in tongues) but that is only one characte<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Given this is set in a small town in the South, there is some fundamentalism (actually pentecostals speaking in tongues) but that is only one character. The author has beautifully shown the diversity within the three characters and how very different their background, ideals and outlook on life is, despite having grown up in the same town. <br /><br />It doesn't matter who you are, where you come from, and definitely has nothing to do with theism/atheism - it is a simple story of people from different backgrounds fighting for what they believe in, and fighting to create a better life for themselves being true to who they are. They fight to not let guilt and whether it is family, religion, society, beliefs, get in the way of their happiness and peace. Such a brilliant book!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1815256659" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1815256659" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1815256659?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553524024" href="/book/show/25739107-the-serpent-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2016">gr_awards_2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1815256659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9238420575648134435">Warning: This review will risk some controversy! Just remember if you read it that I approach everything with an open mind and that I know that my opinion does not match everyone’s – meaning I know that we are all different and I would not argue with people on here to prove that my opinion is correct.<br/><br/>Overall, I thought this was a great book. It was very easy to read. The story was creative and the characters were interesting. At times, emotions ran high and it hit my feels in all the right place</span>
  <span id="freeText9238420575648134435" style="display:none">Warning: This review will risk some controversy! Just remember if you read it that I approach everything with an open mind and that I know that my opinion does not match everyone’s – meaning I know that we are all different and I would not argue with people on here to prove that my opinion is correct.<br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a great book. It was very easy to read. The story was creative and the characters were interesting. At times, emotions ran high and it hit my feels in all the right places. I think that it is one of the better YA books that I have read recently.<br /><br />Now . . . the controversy! Remember, in my profile I mention that I don’t like to get into arguments over religion. I just think this is very relevant to this book and would not mind an open discussion about it. (Trolls need not apply!)<br /><br />One of the things plaguing the world recently is stereotyping religions. On TV, on the internet, in comments sections, etc. people are made to feel bad because of their religion. Also, the few people who are doing religion wrong or crazy are ruining it for the rest of us! One thing I have seen is Christians depicted as intolerant and judgmental with crazy beliefs that they force on the whole world. As part of their daily activities, they mention God and finding Jesus to everyone they meet and look down severely on anyone who does not agree with them. <br /><br />I am a Christian and none of this describes me. I enjoy the solace that my religion gives me, but I don’t spend time judging others and telling people they are wrong because they are not like me. I believe in science and evolution. I feel like debates to prove whether religion is right or wrong are silly and only serve to perpetuate malice between people who have a difference of opinion. I think those of you who have known me on here for a while know that I read a variety of books, have a variety of friends, and I am kind to all. I get frustrated when I see everything blamed on Christians and worry that if people know I am a Christian they will think that I am part of the problem. But, I am not ashamed of what I am – Christianity should be about love and not hate and I try to live my life every day to make sure that describes me.<br /><br />Okay . . . so the reason that I am ranting . . . this book leans really heavy on the side of Christians being intolerant nutjobs that are not very accepting of those not like them; that they are likely to do strange things in their church, molest children, refuse to let their kids be friends with non-Christians (or not be happy about it if they are), etc. I was hoping that maybe by the end of the book some middle ground would have been reached to show that not all Christianity is like that, but it doesn’t really. It makes me a bit sad because this is a great book that I could see a lot of people reading and I don’t want them to come out of it with that negative viewpoint!<br /><br />Just remember – just like not all Muslims are terrorists, not all Christians are intolerant, hateful jerks!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9238420575648134435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1500886834" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1500886834" />
    <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys"><img alt="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463498958p2/1053760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1500886834?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=ripped-out-my-dang-heart">ripped-out-my-dang-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=hick-grit-lit">hick-grit-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=made-my-face-rain">made-my-face-rain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1500886834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4171395276283625025">This book just knocked a whole lot of books down on my favorites list and it's a young adult book. It's one of my top books ever and I'm terrified to review it because I'm so scared that I can't do it any justice and I want everyone to read this book. <br/><br/><b>People live quiet lives and that's okay. There's dignity in that, no matter what you may think.</b><br/><br/>Set in a rural Tennessee small town that was named after a big wig in the KKK the story takes place over one year. One year in the life of three teenager</span>
  <span id="freeText4171395276283625025" style="display:none">This book just knocked a whole lot of books down on my favorites list and it's a young adult book. It's one of my top books ever and I'm terrified to review it because I'm so scared that I can't do it any justice and I want everyone to read this book. <br><br><b>People live quiet lives and that's okay. There's dignity in that, no matter what you may think.</b><br><br>Set in a rural Tennessee small town that was named after a big wig in the KKK the story takes place over one year. One year in the life of three teenagers that are in their last year of highschool. <br><br>Travis is a big guy that dresses all in black with a dragon necklace and his homemade staff. He wants to take that dang staff everywhere he goes. He is obsessed with a fantasy book series called Bloodfall and except for his two friends Dill and Lydia, he would rather live in his fantasy world and escape his abusive father.<br><b>"Rest, O Knight, proud in victory, proud in death. Let your name evermore be a light to those who loved you. Let white flowers grow upon this place that you rest. Yours was a life well lived, and now you dine in the halls of the Elders at their eternal feast."<br>"I had no idea those books meant that much to you Travis," Lydia murmured. "Now I fell all bad about making all those Bloodfall jokes."<br>"Does that mean you'll read them?"<br>"No."</b><br><br>Lydia is that free spirit. Her family is actually pretty well off and very supportive, but Lydia doesn't fit in with the small town Bible belt because she can't conform. She wears eclectic clothing and is sarcastic to almost being abrasive. She runs a blog on fashion advice called <i>Dollywould</i>. Lydia can not wait to get out of this hick town and take on the world.<br><br>Then you have Dill. Dill's preacher dad recently went to prison. Not for having his congregation handle copperheads and rattlesnakes or even for having them drink strychnine, but Dill's mom and of course his dad blame Dill for him ending up in prison. Dill hates life in the town and is teased and ridiculed because of who his father is. He and his mom swim in debt that his father left them and his Jesus freak mom can't wait for Dill to quit school and help her share some of the load of his father's bills. The only shining lights in Dill's life are his two friends and Lydia is leaving soon. <br><br>That is just a small peek at these characters. Because they all three are just so much more.<br><br>The author of this book writes this whole living in a small southern town to absolute perfection. The people, the setting, the smells in the air. Perfection. Then the whole having a dad in prison thing. My real life involved that and he completely wrapped me in this story. Even though my story was many years ago..I felt for this kid so much. <br>And depression. He describes that sinking cesspool of depression like I've never read before. If you haven't had a time in your life where you just could not get out of bed and make yourself function..this book puts you there. <br>But it's not just that. Don't think it's just a "head in the oven" book. It's a book about feeling trapped and moving on. Feeling you can't do what others say you can't and moving on. Standing up for yourself and moving on. It's about that light still shining.<br><br><b>"I read somewhere that a lot of the stars we see don't exist anymore. They've already died and it's taken millions of years for their light to reach Earth," Dill said. <br>"That wouldn't be a bad way to die," Lydia said. "Giving off light for million of years after you're gone."</b><br><br>I'm probably going to have to restrict myself from coming and looking at reviews for this book..because for the first time ever it's a book that I would want to troll someone for hating. I wouldn't do that because then I would be an asshole but I love this one just that much.<br>I was reading it last night and trying to keep from tears coming down my face and I looked and my husband had noticed. We are that weirdo family who make fun of each other for stuff like that...it's how we roll. He actually said he was surprised watching my face read this book. He said he had seen all my emotions go across my face. I couldn't even explain to him why I loved this book so much without sobbing. I think I am either menopausal or going crazy. I'm not a crier. I cried all through this dang book even though it's not entirely sad. The writing did that to me. <br><br>Jeff Zentner is a musician..who decided that he would write a book. It's hard for me to wrap my head around the fact that THIS book is his first book. I will rabidly pick up anything this guy puts out. He wants to write something on a napkin and throw it in the trash. I will dig in that trash and treasure that dirty napkin. Stop judging me.<br><br>Everybody just go read this book so that I'll shut up. I'm embarrassing my own damn self.<br><br> <i>Netgalley in exchange for review</i><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455027784i/18044654.jpg" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1102861654?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">this review </a> for this book so much. She gets this book. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4171395276283625025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873172705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2398575754201095926">I wrote this book, and I'm giving it five stars--not because I think it's a flawless book. Rather, because in it, I was able to say exactly what I wanted to say, tell the exact story I needed to tell, and because Dill, Lydia, and Travis were born into the world exactly as they came to me in my mind.<br/><br/>I'm giving it five stars because it has resulted in my meeting the most amazing people--readers, booksellers, teachers, librarians, bloggers, reviewers, other authors--and making some of the best frie</span>
  <span id="freeText2398575754201095926" style="display:none">I wrote this book, and I'm giving it five stars--not because I think it's a flawless book. Rather, because in it, I was able to say exactly what I wanted to say, tell the exact story I needed to tell, and because Dill, Lydia, and Travis were born into the world exactly as they came to me in my mind.<br /><br />I'm giving it five stars because it has resulted in my meeting the most amazing people--readers, booksellers, teachers, librarians, bloggers, reviewers, other authors--and making some of the best friends I've ever had.<br /><br />I'm giving it five stars because it allowed me to reach the audience I most wanted to reach: young people.<br /><br />I'm giving it five stars because it changed my life permanently for the better in more ways than I can count.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2336718338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336718338" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2336718338?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1810757478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5027445732570898646"><b>THIS. FREAKING. BOOK!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457749527ra/18398518.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I loved it sooooooooooooooo much. It broke my freaking heart and gave me joy and broke my heart some more. It's just so wonderful! And the feels in this book are beyond what I can say in my pitiful little review. All I know is if you have been meaning to read this book and have been putting if off, READ IT - you just might find it as wonderful as I did. <br/><br/>The main characters are, Dill, Travis and Lydia and I love them so much! They are so</span>
  <span id="freeText5027445732570898646" style="display:none"><b>THIS. FREAKING. BOOK!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457749527ra/18398518.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved it sooooooooooooooo much. It broke my freaking heart and gave me joy and broke my heart some more. It's just so wonderful! And the feels in this book are beyond what I can say in my pitiful little review. All I know is if you have been meaning to read this book and have been putting if off, READ IT - you just might find it as wonderful as I did. <br><br>The main characters are, Dill, Travis and Lydia and I love them so much! They are some of the most awesome characters I have read in awhile. Dill is the son of the crazy, snake, preacher man. Travis is a fantasy book fanatic whom you can not help but love. He goes around with his dragon necklace and his staff and is constantly reading his favorite author's books. And Lydia is the one that has the money with a father as a dentist and I think her mom was in real estate. Either way, her parents are wonderful people, the boys parents, not so much. <br><br>Dill's preacher father ends up in jail for reasons. And Dill's mom doesn't even want Dill to finish his last year of high school or go to college, because of reasons. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479424649i/21189268._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Travis has a really sweet mom but a jerk for a father. He's a drunk and he's always calling Travis names etc. <br><br>Lydia runs a very popular blog (&lt;---I wish I did) talking about any and everything. She's going to go to college and make something of herself. The boys, not so much, but they finally came up with their own plan. And poor Dill has a crush on Lydia but don't want to tell her. It all eventually comes out when other things happen. And Lydia made me laugh hysterically many times while reading this book! (thank you, Lydia, I needed that)<br><br>Dill is also a brilliant singer/songwriter/guitarist. <br><br>As much as I loved these characters and this book, there were some parts that just ripped my heart out and threw it on the floor. <br><br>I really have nothing else to say about it without giving out spoilers. I had all of this stuff I wanted to say while reading it and I should have written them all down. I would have like to put my many feels in the book, but then again, I would have had to add spoilers and I don't like to do that unless they are mild. There is nothing much mild to this book. <br><br>I hope many more people love this book as much as I did and I cried a few times and laughed a few times. The perfect book, okay . . . not so much the crying because I'm tired of crying in books! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463068710i/19079330.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fin ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/11/the-serpent-king-by-jeff-zentner.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1816340398?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1816340398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8001870202069781320">‘‘The Serpent King’’ is absolutely captivating.<br/><br/>It’s sad but it’s also very inspiring. Jeff Zentner wrote a debut novel here worthy of your shelves, time and attention. <br/><br/>It’s original in a way that is realistic. The characters—Dill, Lydia and Travis—have an authentic voice. They are quite different one from the other, yet they are as thick as thieves. <br/><br/>Dill is a musician, struggling daily with the effects of the sins of his father, literally. His father whom is now behind bars. <br/><br/>Travis’s brother die</span>
  <span id="freeText8001870202069781320" style="display:none">‘‘The Serpent King’’ is absolutely captivating.<br /><br />It’s sad but it’s also very inspiring. Jeff Zentner wrote a debut novel here worthy of your shelves, time and attention. <br /><br />It’s original in a way that is realistic. The characters—Dill, Lydia and Travis—have an authentic voice. They are quite different one from the other, yet they are as thick as thieves. <br /><br />Dill is a musician, struggling daily with the effects of the sins of his father, literally. His father whom is now behind bars. <br /><br />Travis’s brother died, which changed his father enormously, so much that he became verbally and physically abusive.<br /><br />And Lydia, well, she has no money problems, no family problems—in fact, she’s got it pretty easy compared to everybody else, but she needs to learn to accept her friends as they are. She isn’t done growing up, either.<br /><br />It’s a poignant coming-of-age novel that is reminiscent of ‘‘The Perks of Being a Wallflower.’’ <br /><br />Unlike the title and perhaps cover may suggest, and unlike I first thought, there is no magical realism. Everything is very much realistic, unfortunately. No matter where you live—New York, Montréal, Budapest, a random small town no one knows of—you cannot escape life, meaning that bad things happen to everyone, all over the world. <br /><br />But you can decide whether to get up or stay down. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8001870202069781320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2206334176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2206334176" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68050592-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508609296p2/68050592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2206334176?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/68050592-lori">Lori</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2206334176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8480255755132752568">Another great coming of age story!<br/>Warning contents may contain spoilers!<br/>The religious beliefs are part of the background. I didn't get the impression that the author was anti-Christian, nor even especially opposed to snake handling as an expression of faith. There are communities where it is a demonstration of belief. Dill's life is in one. In a lot of ways, it’s the least of his problems. His father is Pastor Early.<br/><blockquote>It had thoroughly scandalized Forestville, Tennessee when Pastor Early of the Ch</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8480255755132752568" style="display:none">Another great coming of age story!<br />Warning contents may contain spoilers!<br />The religious beliefs are part of the background. I didn't get the impression that the author was anti-Christian, nor even especially opposed to snake handling as an expression of faith. There are communities where it is a demonstration of belief. Dill's life is in one. In a lot of ways, it’s the least of his problems. His father is Pastor Early.<br /><blockquote>It had thoroughly scandalized Forestville, Tennessee when Pastor Early of the Church of Christ’s Disciples with Signs of Belief went to the state penitentiary—and not for the reasons anyone expected. Everyone assumed he’d get in trouble someday for the twenty-seven or so rattlesnakes and copperheads his congregants passed around each Sunday. No one knew with certainty what law they were breaking, but it seemed unlawful somehow. And the Tennessee Department of Wildlife did take custody of the snakes after his arrest. Or people thought perhaps he’d run afoul of the law by inducing his flock to drink diluted battery acid and strychnine; another favored worship activity. But no, he went to Riverbend Prison for a different sort of poison: possession of more than one hundred images depicting a minor engaged in sexual activity. </blockquote><br />A lot of the small-town rumor and speculation aimed at Dill. Guilt by association. Some people assume that he lied in court to protect himself. A man of God would never do something so wrong. Dill’s mother would prefer to believe that it was his porn. Both of his parents blame Dill for his father’s imprisonment. A minor would not have been prosecuted. If Dill had claimed the porn, then his father would not be in prison, and they wouldn’t be in debt. His father rationalizes his imprisonment as being part of God’s plan. I’m here because the Lord wanted me to minister to other inmates. Their emotional blackmail on this kid is relentless.<br />While it’s wrapped in scripture, I just thought that they’re selfish and self-serving. Your child’s best interest should come before your own. Expecting him to lie and perjure himself to protect his father’s sin and crime is not an aspect of Christ mission fulfilled on earth. Ministry to the imprisoned is one of the Corporal Works of Mercy that Christians perform. I understand that the prison is distant, but that’s why church groups organize bus trips for community outreach.<br />On the bright side, Dill has a couple of friends. Travis’ story broke my heart. And, I liked Lydia and her parents. She’s not completely likable, but a plausible enough character. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8480255755132752568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1476740197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1476740197" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476740197?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476740197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17823363372522242422"><b>THERE ARE NO WORDS TO DESCRIBE HOW FREAKING AMAZING THIS BOOK IS AND HOW MUCH I ADORE IT.</b> Well, wait. I will use words. Psychotic words most likely BUT WORDS because <i>omg I loved this book so much.</i> It is gut-wrenching and precious and inspiring and hopeful and <b>balances darkness and hope using some of the best storytelling I've experienced in a long time.</b> There is not enough FLAILING in the world for how much I want to FLAIL RIGHT NOW.<br/><br/>Shout out to this book for existing! Shout out to it for smashi</span>
  <span id="freeText17823363372522242422" style="display:none"><b>THERE ARE NO WORDS TO DESCRIBE HOW FREAKING AMAZING THIS BOOK IS AND HOW MUCH I ADORE IT.</b> Well, wait. I will use words. Psychotic words most likely BUT WORDS because <i>omg I loved this book so much.</i> It is gut-wrenching and precious and inspiring and hopeful and <b>balances darkness and hope using some of the best storytelling I've experienced in a long time.</b> There is not enough FLAILING in the world for how much I want to FLAIL RIGHT NOW.<br><br>Shout out to this book for existing! Shout out to it for smashing my <i>heart</i> and then being so inspiring I think I need to go eat a planet in celebration.<br><br><b>It's basically a story of survival and friendship in a backwards country town.</b> It's narrated by three teens, <b>Dill, Lydia, and Travis</b> and usually I don't like that many POVs. bUt omg. Each person was <i>complex</i> and interesting and loveable and heartbreaking. I love love <i>loved</i> them all. LIKE DON'T EVEN ASK ME TO CHOOSE A FAVOURITE.<br><br><b> • DILL:</b> he's the son of a preacher who's just been imprisoned for sexual charges and EVERYBODY knows Dill and is disgusted by him. Tiny town, remember? Country hicks = not very forgiving. His mother hates him, school is hell, he's got NO FUTURE because he's stuck in this town and his best friend Lydia is leaving for college and basically ajfdkaslfda <b>he was tragic and adorable and quiet and nearly broken</b> and I couldn't love him more. He DOES lash out irrationally with passive-aggressive arguments with Lydia. But I get it?!? When you face losing someone, sometimes you push them away first to help dull the pain. BUT IT JUST MADE ME LOVE HIM MORE. Plus he's musical!! Composes!! BLESS THIS BOOK!!<br><b>• LYDIA:</b> she's a super famous fashion blogger and only 17 #NoImNotJealousHaHaHa. And she's fashionable, super sassy, epically fabulous, definitely not skinny, and has a future of success paved out before her. Plus she has the mOST EPIC PARENT-DAUGHTER RELATIONSHIP EVER. The banter with the parents was so spot on!! Omg!! I love how she as flawed <i>and</i> flawless. Trust me, it works. She was a go-getter, but also a dreamer, and her two best-friends were dorks, which automatically means she's a glorious person. Also sorry not sorry but I 100% imagined her as Lydia from Teen Wolf.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477301300ra/20935716.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>• TRAVIS:</b> He was the most adorable dork to ever dork in the universe. He's OBSESSED with fantasy, specifically this trilogy which he can't stop talking about. He's big and kind and unassuming and just downright <i>lovely</i>. Books about lovely boys need to be more of a thing. And he starts writing and just ajfdsakfd I LOVED TRAVIS AND HE WAS SO PRECIOUS AND PERFECT. He had the most horrible dad who abused him and it broke me. 3 He reminded me of Adam from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> but no bitterness, just 100% gorgeous personality despite his horrible homelife.<br><br><b>HOW ARE THESE CHARACTERS ALL SO PRECIOUS????</b> I can't get over the fact that they felt so REAL. I didn't want to ever stop reading this book. And this is only the author's debut?? Sign me up to read anything by Jeff Zentner ever.<br><br><b>Did I mention the writing?!?</b> Flawless. It was heavily dialogue centred and balanced the most HILARIOUS humour ever with purely poignant scenes with words I never want to stop thinking about. But seriously, I laughed out loud several times. HONKED, ACTUALLY. And my dog looked displeased. And <b>any story about three best friends</b> making the best out of bad situations is the kind of story I'm infinitely in love with. It described everything SO WELL. And the contrast?!? Like Lydia's rich family as opposed to Travis' cruel father as opposed to Dill's dying house of poison??? I CAN'T GET OVER HOW VISUALLY AMAZING IT WAS. And heartbreaking. Like, dude. Break my heart. Walk all over it. I don't even mind obviously.<br><br><b>There are religious tones in it too, which concerned me at first....but turned out okay.</b> Like I just avoid religious books avidly. And I don't even know WHAT kind of "Christian" believes in handling snakes and drinking poison but...okay then. But like it didn't slam religion?? It slammed religion that damages people and it laid out how wrong it is to ruin people's lives because of your "religious beliefs". But I just really like how it was all handled. And Dill's father was totally insane. Just sayin'. Please don't touch snakes, kids. DO NOT.<br><br><b>Also it really tackles mental illness and it does so flawlessly.</b> Like depression? This is the kind of book that gets depression 100% right. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I also felt my entire soul <i>lurch</i> when Dill was contemplating suicide after Travis' death. It was so well done and it turned out so freaking hopeful I just...I love this book so much. I'm <i>so glad</i> he didn't jump and he decided to have a better life. Dill is so precious. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>AND IT BROKE ME INTO A MILLION PIECES.</b> As all the good books do, obviously. But seriously, one minute I was laughing and the next I HAD NO AIR.<br><br><b>ALL IN ALL: this books is incredible and everyone everywhere should read it.</b> Immediately. Like gooooooo. This is one of the BEST BOOKS I'VE READ THIS YEAR. I'm not crying, you're crying. It totally stole a piece of my soul and I'm totally okay with that. <b>It was brutal and hopeful</b> which is a combination I want to see more in books. The writing = perfect. The characters = my new best friends. My heart = A MESS.<br><br>I LIKE THIS BOOK A LOT, CAN YOU TELL.<br><br>----- QUOTES ------<br><br><blockquote>Lydia set down her phone and began typing a post about the road trip to Nashville, shopping at Attic, and some thoughts on the first day of school. She got stuck and began looking for ways to procrastinate.</blockquote><br>#HellaRelatable<br><br><blockquote>"And anyway, how is a coffee shop Christian?"<br>"It implies that normal coffee shops are satanic."<br>"Which they totally are. It's like, can I please just get a cup of coffee without having to kneel before Lucifer and pledge my eternal soul?"<br>"Here's your latte. Will that be cash, credit, or the blood of a virgin?"</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>"I had no idea those books meant <i>that</i> much to you, Travis," Lydia murmured. "Now I feel bad about making all those Bloodfall jokes."<br>"Does this mean you'll read them?"<br>"No."</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>"I mean, it's not like she doesn't like <i>anything</i>. It just has to be Christian. Really Christian," Dill said.<br>"Like the Bible barely makes the cut because Christ is only in the second half," Lydia said.<blockquote></blockquote>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10497120891768709983">I feel... overwhelmed and content and broken and hopeful at the same time. <br/>I can’t believe this is Jeff Zentner’s debut novel. I don’t really know how to articulate into words how this story crept up on me without me even realising it and laid itself comfortably within me. These characters and their lives felt real so me and during the course that I was reading this book in, they absolutely became a part of my life and I feel like their stories will linger and it’ll be a source of courage and ho</span>
  <span id="freeText10497120891768709983" style="display:none">I feel... overwhelmed and content and broken and hopeful at the same time. <br />I can’t believe this is Jeff Zentner’s debut novel. I don’t really know how to articulate into words how this story crept up on me without me even realising it and laid itself comfortably within me. These characters and their lives felt real so me and during the course that I was reading this book in, they absolutely became a part of my life and I feel like their stories will linger and it’ll be a source of courage and hope for me, because they have defied their own odds. <br /><br />I feel sick with this heaviness that is sitting on my heart right now and desperately need a book that’ll make me feel light again, because my insides hurt. <br /><br /><b>TRIGGER WARNINGS:</b> emotional/physical abuse and suicide.<br /><br />(Buddy-read with my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/50761363-lucie" rel="nofollow noopener">my lovely lucie!</a>) ❤️</span>

<div id="review_1979111551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979111551" />
    <a title="Annet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166369-annet"><img alt="Annet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380139289p2/1166369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979111551?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annet" href="/user/show/1166369-annet">Annet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=kids">kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=family-ties">family-ties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=hope">hope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166369-annet?shelf=fun-sad-at-the-same-time">fun-sad-at-the-same-time</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979111551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12588327318986548920"><i>And if you're going to live, you might as well do painful, brave and beautiful things... </i><br/><br/>Great book, heartbreaker & feelgood... review to follow. First, to work!<br/>....Home from work! But tired...I'm not as young as the main character youngsters in this book :-) I'll tell this: the book was wonderful until about 60%, then I lost a bit of interest, and it picked up again in the end. Four stars! Story of three young friends final year in college, going to university and knowing they will go their dif</span>
  <span id="freeText12588327318986548920" style="display:none"><i>And if you're going to live, you might as well do painful, brave and beautiful things... </i><br /><br />Great book, heartbreaker &amp; feelgood... review to follow. First, to work!<br />....Home from work! But tired...I'm not as young as the main character youngsters in this book :-) I'll tell this: the book was wonderful until about 60%, then I lost a bit of interest, and it picked up again in the end. Four stars! Story of three young friends final year in college, going to university and knowing they will go their different ways.... an extraordinary combination... Dill, son of imprisoned Pastor Dillard Early Sr., in prison because of child porn.... handler of snakes in his church. Dill is a troubled kid due to this weird situation. Lydia, a mind of her own, successful blogger and fashionista, parents who are well off and love her, who give her space to live her life the way she wants it, and Travis, a big guy with passion for fantasy books &amp; games, abused by his drunk father.... Dill, Lydia and Travis are true friends. The story is really beautiful, leading up to a tragic event about midway in the story.<br />I have to say, after that the story gets a bit mushy, a bit lovey dovey, without giving away too much details. Now that bored me a bit after a while, so the glimmering 4.5&gt;5 stars went back to let's say 3.8 for me. The ending: strong. All in all, an emotional, well written story, grabs you by the heart and yes, ... I cried, lying in my bed reading.... had to stop at one point.<br />So, I've said it before and will say it again, a book that makes me cry must be a good book (unless it is from sheer frustration of course :-)). 4 stars&amp; recommended. My first 'ponderings' about this book... Special.<br /><br />Dill's lyrics:<br /><i>Moonlight. Calm after thunderstorm.<br />Scarecrows. Dusty bibles. Abandoned houses.<br />Fireflies. Sunlight through dust. Fallen leaves. <br />Churchyard cemetery. Gray autumn sky. <br />River levee. Gravel Road. Wind chimes. <br />Wood smoke. Train whistle on winter night.<br />Kudzu on telephone pole. Hymnal falling apart. <br />White crosses by highway. Cicada hum.<br />Shadows. Sparrows. Rust. Railroad crossing<br />lights through fog. Crickets. Dance of leaves <br />in wind. Decaying barn. Field after harvest. <br />Clouds covering moon. Quiet dusk. Lightning. <br />Heartbeats. </i></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2028286714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16463098081620792709">Against a backdrop of rural Tennessee, <i>The Serpent King</i> follows the perspectives of three teens: Dill, Lydia and Travis. <br/><br/>I just love a solid friendship trio!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565795997ra/27993089.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It is their Senior year of high school. The three are struggling to break free of the molds set for them by their parents and other adults. <br/><br/>In addition, they are also exploring who they are as people, independent from their families, and what sort of life they would like to lead.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565795997ra/27993088.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>This story is incredibly moving and deals with some heavy topi</span>
  <span id="freeText16463098081620792709" style="display:none">Against a backdrop of rural Tennessee, <i>The Serpent King</i> follows the perspectives of three teens: Dill, Lydia and Travis. <br><br>I just love a solid friendship trio!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565795997ra/27993089.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is their Senior year of high school. The three are struggling to break free of the molds set for them by their parents and other adults. <br><br>In addition, they are also exploring who they are as people, independent from their families, and what sort of life they would like to lead.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565795997ra/27993088.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This story is incredibly moving and deals with some heavy topics, but all told from an overwhelmingly sensitive voice. <br><br>I was blown away by the quality and style of Jeff Zentner's writing. This book made me feel so much. Yes, me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446930728ra/16928560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It awoke my soul and brought forth every emotion you could possibly imagine. Not only did I laugh out loud but I also cried, <b>
  <u>real actual tears</u>
</b>, just flowing forth like my heart were breaking.<br><br>That's good writing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542120509ra/26589900.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would recommend this story to anyone, particularly those looking to defrost their cold hearts. I wasn't sure what to expect going in and was genuinely surprised by how much this book sucked me in. <br><br>I want more books that feel like this!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440985333ra/16048814.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is important to note that I listened to the audiobook. There were three incredible narrators that melded together into a fantastically seamless production.<br><br>I <u>highly recommend</u> the audio!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543105511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16955964481879699882">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“If you’re going to live, you might as well do painful, brave, and beautiful things.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>A week or so ago I claimed that it would be hard to top <i>Dark Matter</i> as my best read of 2016. Turns out I lied. It wasn’t that hard at all. Once again <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1500886834?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shelby</a> (or more specifically, her NetGalley addiction) gets the credit for putting this one on my radar. She’s a horrible old bitty like me and rarely gives out the 5 Stars so when she raved about <i>The</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16955964481879699882" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“If you’re going to live, you might as well do painful, brave, and beautiful things.”</i>
</b><br><br>A week or so ago I claimed that it would be hard to top <i>Dark Matter</i> as my best read of 2016. Turns out I lied. It wasn’t that hard at all. Once again <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1500886834?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelby</a> (or more specifically, her NetGalley addiction) gets the credit for putting this one on my radar. She’s a horrible old bitty like me and rarely gives out the 5 Stars so when she raved about <i>The Serpent King</i> (well, in all honesty it was when she posted a non giff-i-fied review) I knew I should take her seriously. I think she has emotions a little more often than I do, though, so I was <b>positive</b> my robot heart could make it through <i>The Serpent King</i> unscathed. After all . . . . <br> <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457643768ra/18384138.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then I met Dill, a boy whose daddy was famous for being a snake-handling/strychnine drinking preacher, but has most recently become famous for activities most of us only see on Dateline. It was impossible not to immediately want to tuck Dill into a special corner of my heart . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“No Jesus, no peace. Know Jesus, know peace. What if you know Jesus but have no peace?”</i>
</b><br><br>Dill introduced me to Lydia – a girl who marched to the beat of her own drum and somehow managed to be best friends with Dill although she didn’t quite share his love for the Lord . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Do you think that’s what Jesus really meant? Maybe he was like, ‘and theoretically, you could probably pick up snakes,’ and Mark’s over there writing and he’s like, ‘You should literally pick up snakes. Cool, Jesus, got it!’ And Jesus is going, ‘Well, calm down with the snake business. Don’t be weird; just be a decent person. It’s really more of a metaphor.’ And Mark is writing, ‘Definitely pick up actual literal snakes and drink actual real poison like rotten grape juice or other Bible-y poison.’”</i>
</b><br><br>(It probably goes without saying that Lydia was my people.)<br><br>Then the two kids introduced me to the final member of their trifecta – a boy named Travis who found what he believed in through a different sort of good book . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457643768ra/18384139.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I can’t remember the last time a book affected me this much or when I read a YA story with multiple narrators who had such distinct voices and personalities. I have placed <i>The Serpent King</i> on the “like-this-or-we-can’t-be-friends” shelf. Normally that title is just for grins, but there’s a good chance if you hate this one I will experience a severe case of the butthurt and not be able to speak to you anymore. (Have no fears, Ron 2.0, you get a pass for not liking <b>anything</b> that I do and all that jazz.) Everyone read this. It feeds my dark side to watch you all cry the ugly tears of a Kardashian, especially if I know you will be like me and look <b>
  <i>“like your heart stepped on a Lego”</i>
</b> once you are finished. As for me, I’ll be uhhhhhhhhhhhhhhhhhhhh busy for awhile . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457643768ra/18384140.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>ARC provided by NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. Thank you, NetGalley!</i><br></span>

<div id="review_1662526142" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662526142" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662526142?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662526142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8130988815017531329">Life is pretty tough for Dill Early. It wasn't always easy growing up as the son of a controversial Pentecostal minister who, along with members of his congregation, handled rattlesnakes and drank poison. But when his father runs afoul of the law and winds up in prison, life gets even harder for Dill. He must deal with the constant bullying of his high school classmates and the suspicion and cruel treatment of former church members and others in his small town of Forrestville, Tennessee.<br/><br/>The futu</span>
  <span id="freeText8130988815017531329" style="display:none">Life is pretty tough for Dill Early. It wasn't always easy growing up as the son of a controversial Pentecostal minister who, along with members of his congregation, handled rattlesnakes and drank poison. But when his father runs afoul of the law and winds up in prison, life gets even harder for Dill. He must deal with the constant bullying of his high school classmates and the suspicion and cruel treatment of former church members and others in his small town of Forrestville, Tennessee.<br /><br />The future looks bleak for Dill—he cannot even begin to consider college because he has to help his mother survive financially, given the mountain of debt they live with since his father's legal troubles occurred. But fortunately, his two best friends, Lydia and Travis—outcasts in their own right—are there to attempt to cheer him up and support him. Lydia, the creator of a fashion and culture blog, can't wait to get out of Forrestville and start a new life, hopefully as a student at NYU. Travis would rather spend time reading and re-reading his favorite series of fantasy books then focus on his own problems, which he has largely kept a secret from his friends.<br /><br />As the end of their senior year in high school draws closer and closer, and Lydia gets more excited about leaving their town behind her, Dill gets more and more upset. He feels as if she'll be happy not only to get out of town, but to get rid of him and Travis, and that hurts him more and more, especially as Dill comes to realize just how strong his feelings are for her. Lydia tries to encourage Dill to think beyond the limits he and his mother have put on his future, tries to make him believe that college is an option. But Dill views her attempts to help as wanting to change him. And as events in their lives go from bad to worse, he's afraid to make himself even more vulnerable, and he doesn't want to jeopardize their relationship.<br /><br />"Because we should do things we're afraid of. It makes it easier every time we do it."<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Serpent King</i>
</b> is a beautiful and moving book, at times bleak and at times hopeful. It absolutely captured my heart and my mind. I loved these characters and their interactions with each other. These characters may be somewhat wise beyond their years but they act like real teenagers—you don't marvel at their dialogue at the same time you wonder whether teenagers really talk this way. I was utterly invested in this story from the very first page, and as much as I wanted to read the whole thing so quickly, I was really sad that it was over when I was finished.<br /><br />This is a book about how we can't let our lives be dictated by our families or our heritage, and we can't let those around us limit our potential. But more than anything, this is a book about friendship and how it frees and changes us, and how we must find the courage to act on our desires and wishes before it's too late.<br /><br />"And if you're going to live, you might as well do painful, brave, and beautiful things."<br /><br />Jeff Zentner is such an assured writer; it's amazing to think this is his debut novel. I really loved this, and once again, I marvel at the amazing talent being demonstrated in the YA genre these days, although this isn't a book just for young adults by any means. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8130988815017531329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1576711252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576711252" />
    <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12058788-2"><img alt="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589380555p2/12058788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576711252?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" href="/user/show/12058788-2">Ɗẳɳ  2.☊</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780553524048" href="/book/show/25738910-the-serpent-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=the-wonder-years">the-wonder-years</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=goldilocks-zone">goldilocks-zone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576711252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11485853701266208656">Some reviews—a pitiful few—seem to write themselves, while others require extensive time to collect my thoughts, or a knock-down-drag-out battle with procrastination. But once in a blue moon, I stumble across a story like this one that’s another animal altogether. <br/><br/>After finishing this book, rather than posting a timely review like a decent little goodreader, I instead teased out an absurd question, “Do I dare slap five stars on a silly little young adult story?” Well . . . now that my emotional </span>
  <span id="freeText11485853701266208656" style="display:none">Some reviews—a pitiful few—seem to write themselves, while others require extensive time to collect my thoughts, or a knock-down-drag-out battle with procrastination. But once in a blue moon, I stumble across a story like this one that’s another animal altogether. <br /><br />After finishing this book, rather than posting a timely review like a decent little goodreader, I instead teased out an absurd question, “Do I dare slap five stars on a silly little young adult story?” Well . . . now that my emotional scars have had sufficient time to heal, I think I’m finally ready to answer that question. Absolutely! Any book that can put me through the wringer—twist me inside out—and run through the whole gamut of human emotions is well-deserving of all the stars. <br /><br /><i>The Serpent King</i> is the story of three friends—three social outcast—and their senior year of high school in the sleepy little backwater town of Forrestville, Tennessee. Travis is a Hodor sized Lord of the Rings type uber-nerd, fond of dressing like a wizard and carrying an oaken staff. Lydia is a straight-A student with a popular fashion blog, who’s counting down the days until her real life can begin at NYU. But it’s Dill who’s the heart and soul of the book. A fledgling musician caught between a rock and a hard place—living in two worlds, but a part of neither. On one side is his father’s congregation, and on the other is the rest of the town that looks down their nose at their weird snake-handling faith. As the pastor’s son, it would have been a challenge to fit into high school as it was, but to make matters worse his father’s sent off to prison for peddling in kiddie porn, and it was his Dill’s own testimony that was responsible for putting him away. Reviled by the flock for refusing to take the blame, when his father insisted that the computer photos were Dill’s, and shunned by the community for his faith and family, Dill’s only solace is the love and support of his best friends. <br /><br /><b> “He squinted to read the sign out of habit. ‘No Jesus, No Peace. Know Jesus, Know Peace.’ What if you know Jesus but have no peace? Does that mean the sign is wrong, or does that mean you don’t know Jesus quite as well as you think?”</b><br /><br />Through an alternating point of view narrative, we soon discover how remarkable those friendships are. And the greater the outside pressure, teasing, and bullying—from both classmates and parents—the stronger their bonds become. <br /><br />Dill’s resigned to his fate though, completely closed off to the idea of ever escaping this awful place. With his dad in prison and his mom barely scraping by, it’s up to Dill to pick up the slack, so his chance at college and creating a better life for himself is virtually nil. However, with the clock ticking down to the day when Lydia will walk out of his life forever, a tragedy strikes that shakes him to the very foundation of his being . . .<br /><br />This book was an emotional roller-coaster. It wasn’t the tragedy so much as the fallout that left such a lasting impression on me. <b>“Something broke loose inside Dill’s mind. Something that had been moored against the roaring tumult. It came untethered and crashed around with reckless abandon—burning, shattering, consuming. He stopped seeing color and all became a swirling, howling, leaden gray desolation. But the pain hadn’t arrived. The way the sea recedes before a tsunami, so every part of him receded. And then the pain struck.”</b> Watching as the characters attempt to cope in the aftermath is what separated the story from countless other young adult dramas, in my mind, and elevated the narrative into something truly special. <br /><br />What’s weird is that I tend to shy away from the young adult section of the library because most stories are riddled with one or more of the following: teen-angst, clichéd narratives, sparkly vampire love triangles, special snowflakes, dystopian savior complexes, or suicide glorification. Honestly, what self-respecting middle-aged man still reads that shit? However, I am a sucker for coming of age tales, and this one managed to snare me in its web rather quickly, with pitch-perfect dialog, numerous discussions of music and mixtapes, and down-to-earth, relatable characters. <br /><br />In the end, I suppose that’s what it boils down with most stories: much of your love or hate is predetermined by how well you connect with the characters on an emotional level. And this one left me feeling like my <b>“heart had stepped on a Lego.”</b><br /><br />That’s the power of a coming of age story when done right. And this terrific tale of love, loss, and friendship receives my highest recommendation. Five stars . . . full stop.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11485853701266208656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4959200446326380857" style="display:none">Well this was a heart wrencher!!<br /><br /><i> “We need to take care of each other from now on. We need to be each other’s family because ours are so messed up. We need to make better lives for ourselves. We gotta start doing stuff we’re afraid to do.” </i> <br /><br />I’d heard great things about this contemporary and I was not disappointed. <br /><br />Told in 3 perspectives. <br />We have Dill, a young musician living in the shadow of his terribly “religious” father - imprisoned for a terrible crime. <br />Travis, who reads an epic fantasy series as an escape from his abusive father. <br />Finally we have Lydia. I didn’t warm to her immediately, in fact I still found a lot of the things she’d say uncomfortable. Mainly the way she’d speak to her parents. But she was a great support to Dill and she definitely had character development. <br /><br />These three teens are best friends as they tackle high school senior year and the lead up to college. And when disaster strikes it proves found family can be just if not more important than blood family. <br /><br />I don’t want to give away too much because of spoilers but I really enjoyed this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I liked that Dill kept his faith despite the awful introduction he had to it from his parents. He found his own version and I thought that was great. I loved Travis’ character - and his death broke me 😭.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Overall a solid YA with some important messages.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4959200446326380857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4256790297608758392"><i>Full review posted:</i><br/><br/>I have no idea how I’m going to convey all the feelings this book gave me into coherent words…do I really have to??<br/><br/><i> Times are simpler when no one hates you because of your name and it doesn’t occur to you to be ashamed of it. </i><br/><br/>This book tells the story of our three characters: <br/>1)	An internet famous fashion icon who is unapologetically herself<br/>2)	A tragic boy shackled in his father’s shadow<br/>3)	A burly lumberjack of a boy who is made from marshmallow and sprinkles and deserves ever</span>
  <span id="freeText4256790297608758392" style="display:none"><i>Full review posted:</i><br /><br />I have no idea how I’m going to convey all the feelings this book gave me into coherent words…do I really have to??<br /><br /><i> Times are simpler when no one hates you because of your name and it doesn’t occur to you to be ashamed of it. </i><br /><br />This book tells the story of our three characters: <br />1)	An internet famous fashion icon who is unapologetically herself<br />2)	A tragic boy shackled in his father’s shadow<br />3)	A burly lumberjack of a boy who is made from marshmallow and sprinkles and deserves everything beautiful and happy <br /><br />This is not a fun book, this book is more likely to split you in half than to make you smile (though it definitely has its funny moments) <br /><br />-	Our three main characters live in a very…fundamentally religious town that is harsh and unforgiving to those who need it most<br />-	It’s such a great story of friendship and hope and acceptance and it plunges that knife deep, deep down into your being <br />-	Ft. Wholesome friendships<br /><blockquote> <i>Dill angled one of the vents toward his face. “You ever think about how weird it is that Earth is hurtling through the black vacuum of space, where it’s like a thousand below zero, and meanwhile we’re down here sweating?”<br /><br />“I often think about how weird it is that Earth is hurtling through the black vacuum of space and meanwhile you’re down here being a total weirdo.” </i></blockquote><br />-	Basically all the kids in the book have some sort of form of daddy issues (mainly bc their dads are THE BIGGEST JERKS TO EXIST ON THE FACE OF THE EARTH) and so I have taken it upon myself to adopt them <s>that includes lydia, even tho her parents are pretty cool</s> <br />-	All three characters are the most precious little beans you’ve ever witnessed and after reading 13 words from the book, you’re going to be warming up some hot milk and gathering bubble wrap to encapsulate them in <br />-	There’s no incandescent beauties in this book. And I LOVED that. It’s so real, they’re so real, theyre love for each other is so real, you can genuine feel how lost and broken they are without each other and that’s just…something special man <br />-	Now the writing is fantastic. It is heartfelt and dismal and so so so raw. <br />-	The dynamics of the town, the tightness that the characters feel is expressed so perfectly, idk how this is possible to do<br />-	It’s not all sadness either. Like the characters themselves are really funny (when they aren’t being tragic and smol)<br />-	AND THEN<br />-	*IT* HAPPENS<br />-	AND YOU FEEL YOUR HEART BEING TORN OUT OF YOUR BODY<br />-	:) :) :) :) :) :) :) :)<br />-	I can’t say anything beyond I cried until I got a headache and then even when the sadness was over and the happiness was sorta there, I cried even more bc wow I’m an emotional wreck thanks @ author<br />-	<s>youre an evil man</s><br />-	There’s so many parts of this book I cannot even begin to explain all the intricacies it covers but just like, read it if you haven’t already okay. <br /><br /><i>"I had no idea those books meant that much to you, Travis," Lydia murmured. "Now I feel bad about making all those Bloodfall jokes."<br />"Does this mean you'll read them?"<br />"No."</i><br /><br />4.5 stars!!</span>
